  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_94c8d933-76b7-4f89-9b2b-e47f1295d3b3'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer11553116382756220449">In a city that runs on a dwindling supply of magic, a young boy is drawn into a life of wizardry and adventure.   <span id="freeText11553116382756220449" style="display:none">In a city that runs on a dwindling supply of magic, a young boy is drawn into a life of wizardry and adventure. Conn should have dropped dead the day he picked Nevery's pocket and touched the wizard's locus magicalicus, a stone used to focus magic and work spells. But for some reason he did not. Nevery finds that interesting, and he takes Conn as his apprentice on the provision that the boy find a locus stone of his own. But Conn has little time to search for his stone between wizard lessons and helping Nevery discover who or what is stealing the city of Wellmet's magic.</span>

The character development wasn't that good but I did like some of the characters at the end. I didn't feel any attachment to the characters at all except for the protagonist. But I really really enjoyed reading this and it is very humorous. It's still a good book.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer18463692" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer13398996883101552342">This book made me absurdly and enormously happy.<br/><br/><i>The Magic Thief</i> has a number of familiar fantasy motifs and character types. But in <a href='http://www.sarah-prineas.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Sarah Prineas</a>'s hands a story that could have been predictable instead has a wonderful freshness and vitality about it. The invented world in which Conn moves has a Dickensian flair without being merely alt-Victoriana, and its magical system is both well imagined and intriguing. <br/><br/>The characters in <i>The Magic Thief</i> are realistically flawed and fallible, yet they never </span>
  <span id="freeText13398996883101552342" style="display:none">This book made me absurdly and enormously happy.<br /><br /><i>The Magic Thief</i> has a number of familiar fantasy motifs and character types. But in <a href="http://www.sarah-prineas.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Sarah Prineas</a>'s hands a story that could have been predictable instead has a wonderful freshness and vitality about it. The invented world in which Conn moves has a Dickensian flair without being merely alt-Victoriana, and its magical system is both well imagined and intriguing. <br /><br />The characters in <i>The Magic Thief</i> are realistically flawed and fallible, yet they never lost my interest or (where appropriate) my sympathy; I particularly liked the way that Prineas developed a couple of the secondary characters, subverting my expectations of them in a surprising and satisfying way. And her hero -- well. I have a weakness for thieves to begin with, but by the end of the first chapter I was grinning idiotically (always a good sign) and I knew that I was going to like Conn very much indeed.<br /><br /><i>The Magic Thief</i> will be out this June, it's the first of a trilogy, and it's wonderful. If you enjoy quick-paced, engaging MG fantasy, you won't regret preordering this one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13398996883101552342" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <span id="reviewTextContainer760872071" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3026128203931947321">Hmm. It's a fun, fluffy book for MG readers who enjoyed the Harry Potter and Percy Jackson books. The illustrations on the inside are reminiscent of <a href='http://www.marygrandpre.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>Mary GrandPré's</a> Potter artwork, yet it does get repetitive as the same pictures are shown over and over again instead of individual designs for each chapter.<br/><br/>The wizards in this universe must let a magical object choose them in order to access their powers, but instead of a wand it's a stone called the magilicus locus (which just so happens to work e</span>
  <span id="freeText3026128203931947321" style="display:none">Hmm. It's a fun, fluffy book for MG readers who enjoyed the Harry Potter and Percy Jackson books. The illustrations on the inside are reminiscent of <a href="http://www.marygrandpre.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Mary GrandPré's</a> Potter artwork, yet it does get repetitive as the same pictures are shown over and over again instead of individual designs for each chapter.<br><br>The wizards in this universe must let a magical object choose them in order to access their powers, but instead of a wand it's a stone called the magilicus locus (which just so happens to work exactly like a wand in Harry Potter).<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1405354330i/10385496._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There seems to be a little bit of a steampunk element to it as well as many of the characters wear victorian garb and there are clockwork devices to measure and trap magical energy, which is a major plot point towards the end of the novel.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1405355520i/10385636.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Since it's a kid's fantasy book, I guess it wouldn't be complete without twee names like Periwinkle. Can we just discuss for a moment why most of these kinds of books have a character named <b>Periwinkle</b>?<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1405355682ra/10385668.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I think the main thing that sets the Potter books apart from most of the other series with <i>very</i> similar tropes is that Rowling had a warmth to her writing; she allowed us to connect with characters and become engrossed in her world. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/827236.Sarah_Prineas" title="Sarah Prineas" rel="nofollow noopener">Sarah Prineas</a> and many others can use the same themes but you just don't get as invested. Perhaps I'm asking too much from a MG book. Perhaps I'm measuring all other books in the genre against Potter, but really who doesn't?</span>
  <a data-text-id="3026128203931947321" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer21381421" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer717200042896778847"> Conn just wanted some money to pay for his meal when he picked a wizard, Nevery's, pocket. Taking Nevery's locus magicalicus (a stone that helps wizards to focus when using magic) should have caused Conn to die. But he didn't. Nevery finds this interesting, and takes Conn in as his apprentice (more of a servant, though.)<br/> Life is still difficult for Conn even though he gets fed, has a roof over his head, and he even learns how to read. There is contempt for him since he is a known thief and lock</span>
  <span id="freeText717200042896778847" style="display:none"> Conn just wanted some money to pay for his meal when he picked a wizard, Nevery's, pocket. Taking Nevery's locus magicalicus (a stone that helps wizards to focus when using magic) should have caused Conn to die. But he didn't. Nevery finds this interesting, and takes Conn in as his apprentice (more of a servant, though.)<br /> Life is still difficult for Conn even though he gets fed, has a roof over his head, and he even learns how to read. There is contempt for him since he is a known thief and lock pick. The city that he lives in has a dwindling supply of magic. He is given only 30 days by the Magisters to find his OWN locus magicalicus for himself. He knows that it is not in his academicos' stores.<br /><br /> The Magic Thief was an amazing book, and I really loved reading it. I could hardly put it down once I started reading it. Conn is an interesting character, and I liked how, despite his pick-pocketing and thieving ways, he's still completely honest with Nevery. I loved how Conn is very intelligent; it fit his character completely. I'm excited for the sequel, since the first book was completely satisfying, but still makes me want to read more.<br /></span>

          </span>

<div id="review_23887184" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/23887184" />
    <a title="A.J." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1212747-a-j"><img alt="A.J." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546711482p2/1212747.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/23887184?book_show_action=true">Jun 06, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="A.J." class="user" itemprop="url" name="A.J." href="/user/show/1212747-a-j">A.J.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer23887184" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3033313940785116055">Okay, I guess I'm the first to give this book a review after its official publication date (June 3 or thereabouts). <br/><br/>To begin I think a bit of background is in order, because the 3-star rating I gave is deceptively low. The rating only reflects the book and its success stacked against myself as a reader with particular tastes and preferences. This book is definitely for the kiddies. It isn't designed to thrust itself among the greatest epic fantasy stories ever told, and in the darkness category </span>
  <span id="freeText3033313940785116055" style="display:none">Okay, I guess I'm the first to give this book a review after its official publication date (June 3 or thereabouts). <br /><br />To begin I think a bit of background is in order, because the 3-star rating I gave is deceptively low. The rating only reflects the book and its success stacked against myself as a reader with particular tastes and preferences. This book is definitely for the kiddies. It isn't designed to thrust itself among the greatest epic fantasy stories ever told, and in the darkness category it dips below even the for-everyone-but-especially-for-kids C.S. Lewis Narnia series. That being the case, I was surprised I got through the book as quickly as I did.<br /><br />It reads fast. And when I say fast, I mean this thing ZOOMS by. I was clocking 100-page chunks per sitting with enough time left over to catch up on Battlestar Galactica. There is very little fat in this book. In fact I'd say this is, as far as fantasy goes, the chick at school you suspect might be bulimic but you don't have the guts to tell anyone. At times the pacing was so lightning fast that I almost wanted to put the book aside and simply imagine how the character was feeling about all this craziness going on. But on the happier side of the coin, I was too interested to see what happens next to bother.<br /><br />Armed with a pleasant Tolkein lightness and a charming city which manages to be imaginative even in its simplicity, I can't imagine how any fantasy-loving youngster wouldn't get swept up with Conn, his grumpy master Nevery, and the story of one young wizard-thief's quest to be accepted by those around him in the midst of a city where magic is dying.<br /><br />A wonderful read. Perhaps not in my strike-zone of fantasy stories (I like'em dark), but on a more objective basis, certainly well worth the time. Sure as sure. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3033313940785116055" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_343843711" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/343843711" />
    <a title="Ivonne Rovira" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3803671-ivonne-rovira"><img alt="Ivonne Rovira" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339470651p2/3803671.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/343843711?book_show_action=true">Jun 06, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ivonne Rovira" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ivonne Rovira" href="/user/show/3803671-ivonne-rovira">Ivonne Rovira</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio 9781436137355" href="/book/show/7232246-the-magic-thief">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">to lovers of fantasy, both children and adults</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Ivonne by: </span>
      Bill Wolfe
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3803671-ivonne-rovira?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer343843711" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12614999201565843852">Like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2012967.L_M__Boston' title='L.M. Boston' rel='nofollow noopener'>L.M. Boston</a>'s Green Knowe series, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1020792.Antoine_de_Saint_Exup_ry' title='Antoine de Saint-Exupéry' rel='nofollow noopener'>Antoine de Saint-Exupéry</a>'s <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/157993.The_Little_Prince' title='The Little Prince by Antoine de Saint-Exupéry' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Little Prince</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1069006.C_S__Lewis' title='C.S. Lewis' rel='nofollow noopener'>C.S. Lewis</a>' Narnia Chronicles and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1077326.J_K__Rowling' title='J.K. Rowling' rel='nofollow noopener'>J.K. Rowling</a>'s Harry Potter series, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/827236.Sarah_Prineas' title='Sarah Prineas' rel='nofollow noopener'>Sarah Prineas</a>' <i>The Magic Thief</i> represents a children's book that's bound to be devoured by thousands of adults.<br/><br/>The eponymous thief Conn meets his future magical mentor, wizard Nevery Flinglass, while trying to pick his pocket. Nevery's <i>locus magicalicus</i>, a sort of magical stone that gives a wizard his power, should have killed Conn on the spot</span>
  <span id="freeText12614999201565843852" style="display:none">Like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2012967.L_M__Boston" title="L.M. Boston" rel="nofollow noopener">L.M. Boston</a>'s Green Knowe series, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1020792.Antoine_de_Saint_Exup_ry" title="Antoine de Saint-Exupéry" rel="nofollow noopener">Antoine de Saint-Exupéry</a>'s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/157993.The_Little_Prince" title="The Little Prince by Antoine de Saint-Exupéry" rel="nofollow noopener">The Little Prince</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1069006.C_S__Lewis" title="C.S. Lewis" rel="nofollow noopener">C.S. Lewis</a>' Narnia Chronicles and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1077326.J_K__Rowling" title="J.K. Rowling" rel="nofollow noopener">J.K. Rowling</a>'s Harry Potter series, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/827236.Sarah_Prineas" title="Sarah Prineas" rel="nofollow noopener">Sarah Prineas</a>' <i>The Magic Thief</i> represents a children's book that's bound to be devoured by thousands of adults.<br /><br />The eponymous thief Conn meets his future magical mentor, wizard Nevery Flinglass, while trying to pick his pocket. Nevery's <i>locus magicalicus</i>, a sort of magical stone that gives a wizard his power, should have killed Conn on the spot -- but does not, much to Nevery's amazement. Thus begins a partnership and a trilogy that will attract as many adults as members of its intended middle-grades audience. Their city of Wellmet, like other cities in this alternative fantasy universe, literally runs on magic; recently, that magical force has been gradually disappearing -- almost as if it were being drained by some unseen and unsavory force. Hmmm. While Nevery is investigating the strange diminution, the teenaged Conn undertakes to find his very own <i>locus magicalicus</i>, a requirement if he is ever to become a full-fledged wizard -- or even a full-fledged wizard's apprentice. <br /><br />Prineas navigates the plot through terrifying scrapes and close calls for Conn, his hard-earned advancement in the wizarding realm, a possible newfound love, and a search for the cause of -- and solution to -- what Nevery calls "the decay of magic" in Wellmet. Take some advice from me: Buy the other two books in the trilogy -- <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9814409.The_Magic_Thief_Lost" title="The Magic Thief Lost by Sarah Prineas" rel="nofollow noopener">The Magic Thief: Lost</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9508284.The_Magic_Thief_Found__Magic_Thief__3_" title="The Magic Thief Found (Magic Thief #3) by Sarah Prineas" rel="nofollow noopener">The Magic Thief: Found</a> -- <i>before</i> you finish <i>The Magic Thief</i>. You will thoroughly enjoy the novel and the endearingly sassy and intrepid Conn. How much? So much that you will be eager to pick up Conn's adventures in the sequels just as soon as you finish <i>The Magic Thief</i>. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12614999201565843852" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_76936480" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/76936480" />
    <a title="Kathryn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/446464-kathryn"><img alt="Kathryn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1316545868p2/446464.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/76936480?book_show_action=true">Nov 06, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathryn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathryn" href="/user/show/446464-kathryn">Kathryn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">those seeking good middle-grade fantasy</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/446464-kathryn?shelf=annie-and-katie-bookclub">annie-and-katie-bookclub</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/446464-kathryn?shelf=fantasy-sci-fi">fantasy-sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/446464-kathryn?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer76936480" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3131886254676656538">Conn is a young thief in the Twilight, managing to stay alive and well when so many others have fared far worse in the cold and threadbare conditions. But, when he tries to steal a wizard's locus magicalius stone (a source of connection with the source of magic) he ends up winning a new life for himself as an apprentice to the wizard Nevery. For Nevery sees what others never bothered to see in the lowly pick-pocket; a good-hearted boy with an uncanny aptitude for magic. But even in Nevery's home</span>
  <span id="freeText3131886254676656538" style="display:none">Conn is a young thief in the Twilight, managing to stay alive and well when so many others have fared far worse in the cold and threadbare conditions. But, when he tries to steal a wizard's locus magicalius stone (a source of connection with the source of magic) he ends up winning a new life for himself as an apprentice to the wizard Nevery. For Nevery sees what others never bothered to see in the lowly pick-pocket; a good-hearted boy with an uncanny aptitude for magic. But even in Nevery's home, life is not exactly cozy and comfortable. The magic is fading throughout Wellmet and even in the Duchesses' Dawn Palace, all is not well. Is the magic fading due to forces of nature, corrupt wizards, or something else? And who will be right when Conn and Nevery begin to disagree on the answer to that question.<br /><br />I really enjoyed the first few chapters of this book. Prineas' wise word choice quickly wove a believable and interesting world. Her use of hyphenated words like "keen-gleam look" really made an interesting style to the story so I became annoyed when, a few chapters in, that style all but disappeared. I felt cheated, as if she tempted us in with promises of being unique and then lapsed back into normalcy. I also felt the first half of the book moved slowly in places, occasionally fell into redundancy or simply failed to really progress the plot or characters. However, I was still interested in our protagonist, his honesty and forthrightness and insight really won me over and I liked that he never made excuses for what he did in the past, never whined or complained for what he had to endure. Some of the other characters, like Nevery, were a bit more "standard fantasy stock" but ultimately wove together to create a satisfying and fresh story. I really ended up enjoying the second half of the story. It became more complex and interesting and I was curious and engaged throughout. That bumped this up to a four-star book for me and I am definitely interested to continue the series. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3131886254676656538" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/140565834?book_show_action=true">Jan 13, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andy" href="/user/show/788733-andy">Andy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer140565834" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2856122235833494697">This book, the first in a trilogy, is a great example of how children’s book publishers are putting out way too many series and lots of bad fantasy in an attempt to make money. Connwaer has lots of street smarts and a skilled pick-pocketing hand. At the start of the story he steals the locus magicalicus of the Wizard Nevery Flinglas. This magical device should kill Conn, but doesn’t. And so, Conn is taken in with interest and some apprehension by the wizard Nevery. Magic abounds in their city of</span>
  <span id="freeText2856122235833494697" style="display:none">This book, the first in a trilogy, is a great example of how children’s book publishers are putting out way too many series and lots of bad fantasy in an attempt to make money. Connwaer has lots of street smarts and a skilled pick-pocketing hand. At the start of the story he steals the locus magicalicus of the Wizard Nevery Flinglas. This magical device should kill Conn, but doesn’t. And so, Conn is taken in with interest and some apprehension by the wizard Nevery. Magic abounds in their city of Wellmet, or at least it used to. Lately, the magic has weakened, and Nevery has come back from exile to try and solve the mystery of its disappearance. Conn is sent to school, he learns to read, longs to become Nevery’s apprentice, and struggles for acceptance. Although Conn must prove that he is worthy of magician status by finding his own locus magicalicus (every true magician has one), he is much more interested in doing his own clandestine detective work to determine where the magic of Wellmet is going. The plot was not engaging and, frankly, rather dumb. The characters were predictable and unoriginal, but worst of all was the writing which lacked vocabulary and eloquence.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2856122235833494697" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_343720286" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/343720286" />
    <a title="Ann Rees" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10041146-ann-rees"><img alt="Ann Rees" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591740140p2/10041146.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/343720286?book_show_action=true">Jun 06, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ann Rees" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ann Rees" href="/user/show/10041146-ann-rees">Ann Rees</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10041146-ann-rees?shelf=insults-intelligence-of-readers">insults-intelligence-of-readers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10041146-ann-rees?shelf=not-worth-a-reread">not-worth-a-reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10041146-ann-rees?shelf=mary-sue-or-gary-stu">mary-sue-or-gary-stu</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10041146-ann-rees?shelf=overrated">overrated</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer343720286" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17820149793042125799">As I was perusing the shelves in my local library, I came upon this book, looking deceptively innocent with its nice blue and gold cover. Since I like fantasy, I decided I'd give it a go. Little did I know what horrors awaited me. The plot, (if you can call it that), centers around a young thief oh so appropriately named Conn, who attempts to steal a locus magilawhatsit from the wizard Nevery, which should have killed him. Unfortunately, this doesn't happen. Instead, Nevery decides to take Conn </span>
  <span id="freeText17820149793042125799" style="display:none">As I was perusing the shelves in my local library, I came upon this book, looking deceptively innocent with its nice blue and gold cover. Since I like fantasy, I decided I'd give it a go. Little did I know what horrors awaited me. The plot, (if you can call it that), centers around a young thief oh so appropriately named Conn, who attempts to steal a locus magilawhatsit from the wizard Nevery, which should have killed him. Unfortunately, this doesn't happen. Instead, Nevery decides to take Conn home with him and make him his apprentice. Because really, when a grubby little thief tries to steal your powerful magical stone from you and doesn't die from it, you would obviously take him in, feed him, clothe him, train him in magic, and send him to an expensive school where he receives an education that most orphans can only dream of. <br /><br />He then begins the search to find his own special magic stone thingy, which he does for most of the book. The plot drags on and on without anything interesting happening besides the numerous boring subplots (except for the biscuit recipe). Conn eventually finds out that 'his' stone is currently in the hands of the queen. Naturally, he decides to sneak into the palace and take it. I mean, it's not like the ruler of the land owns it or anything. Oh wait, she does. But that doesn't matter because it's HIS stone after all. And after he finds his locus magicachoo, he (spoiler) promptly loses it when fighting the bad guy. The magic stone concept strongly resembles the wand one from the Harry Potter series in that the wand/stone chooses the wizard. Except in HP, you feel Harry's emotional connection with his wand, and his devastation when it breaks. Here, you only feel that the whole 'find your magic stone' subplot was a complete and utter waste of time (and paper).<br /><br />'Well,' you ask, 'if the plot isn't the most memorable, surely the characters are original and complex? Or at least likable?' No. Not in the slightest. They are all unpleasant stereotypes you can't connect to. Gary St-err, Conn is your average, badly written fictional thief with a heart of gold. He's 'mischievous', 'quick-witted', 'charming', and has the personality of a doormat. Which is an insult to doormats everywhere. He is such a bland, boring character that I literally forgot his name while reading this book. No joke. If you can't remember what the main character's name is in the middle of the book, you know the author is doing something wrong. <br /><br />Our villain, (whose name I can't remember), is a generic baddie who hates Conn, tries to kill him on various occasions, and has no character whatsoever. The other bad guy (of sorts) is a bully at Conn's school who (surprise, surprise) hates his little pickpocketing guts. He also has no character outside of his stereotyped category. But these are just the antagonists. Doesn't Conn, dull and bland as he is, have any friends? Of course he does. And they also are unoriginal cardboard cut outs. Yay! <br /><br />Nevery is an irascible old codger who, for all his snapping threats at Conn and making him work for his keep (which seems to be a bad thing in Conn's eyes), puts up with his obnoxiousness thinking that he might be useful someday for saving the kingdom or something like that. He is not the best authority figure, particularly when it comes to the way he interacts with others. If handled well, a bad mentor might make for some interesting reading. However, it is not handled well here. <br /><br />You may begin to ask yourself, 'Well, where are all the girl characters? There must be at least one strong female protagonist who helps the hero, right?' Um...if you mean the smart girl who does well in school, and despite being kind of stuck up (spoiler:she's a princess), manages to befriend the hero, then yes, she would probably count as one. Yet another used to death stereotype, Rowan is an intelligent princess who attends Conn's school and helps tutor him, since he can't read or write well, if at all. And is it just me, or is Rowan being set up as Conn's future love interest? Of course, I wouldn't know anything about that considering I haven't read the other two books. <br /><br />Overall impressions? If you couldn't tell from my review, I really don't like this book. The plot (more like a mishmash of subplots) drags in all the wrong places, I've seen all of these characters before, only done better, the writing is nothing great, there aren't any good role models, the world isn't that creative, and all in all it's just very forgettable. There's nothing in this book that makes it worth reading instead of other fantasies. If you do want to read it, I'd advise getting it from the library, so you can see for yourself whether you'd want to buy it or not. There's not a lot that I found morally offensive, but as a fantasy lover I was offended by the number of clichés and recycled ideas that were used here. I have not read the next two books in this series, nor do I plan to. I would only recommend this book to my worst enemies. If you're looking for books about young boys and magic, I suggest you try the Septimus Heap series or reread Harry Potter for the thousandth time.<br /><br />(No disrespect is intended toward the author in this review. I apologize if it seems that way.)<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17820149793042125799" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_148632829" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/148632829" />
    <a title="Ann" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/446509-ann"><img alt="Ann" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1194659951p2/446509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/148632829?book_show_action=true">Feb 16, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ann" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ann" href="/user/show/446509-ann">Ann</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8272374-the-magic-thief">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/446509-ann?shelf=katie-and-annie-bookclub">katie-and-annie-bookclub</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/446509-ann?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/446509-ann?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer148632829" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10181571841844874714">Conn is a common thief, living on the streets of Twilight and stealing what he can to survive. Until he tries to steal something very important from a wizard. But what catches the wizard's interest isn't so much that Conn tried to steal his precious magical stone, but that the stone didn't kill Conn when he tried to.<br/><br/>Twilight is part of a city separated into three sections (basically the good side, the bad side, and the in between), and the city's magic fading - fast. Why? To what effect? And how</span>
  <span id="freeText10181571841844874714" style="display:none">Conn is a common thief, living on the streets of Twilight and stealing what he can to survive. Until he tries to steal something very important from a wizard. But what catches the wizard's interest isn't so much that Conn tried to steal his precious magical stone, but that the stone didn't kill Conn when he tried to.<br /><br />Twilight is part of a city separated into three sections (basically the good side, the bad side, and the in between), and the city's magic fading - fast. Why? To what effect? And how to rectify it are the pressing questions that need to be answered.<br /><br />While a lot of this book is a little predictable, I was still surprised at some of the plot points and found them fairly unique and interesting. <br /><br />This book started a little slow for me. The first two chapters have a very unique writing style, which kind of subsides as the book goes on (though perhaps this is a good thing). But as the story progressed I found myself feeling more and more involved and curious as to how it would end. By the final third of the book I was really enjoying myself and eager to read the next chapter.<br /><br />I liked Prineas' writing style (once the book got into the flow) and the book is easy and quick to get though. I really liked our main character, Conn! He's very likable, smart, brave and observant. I believe my other favorite character was Benet - though to say why would give it away. I liked the other characters a lot, too, but they never really developed as much as I'd hoped, and thus seemed more one-dimensional than the others. Though, I'm hoping this will be alleviated in following books. Which, I do plan to read, and hopefully rather soon!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10181571841844874714" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>,

<span id="freeTextContainer4340749705133713025">2.5<br/><br/>A pretty decent story, if a little typical - orphan boy steals a wizard's locus magicalicus, which should kill him but doesn't. The wizard, intrigued, takes the boy in and the boy just happens to turn out to be a sort of chosen one figure. <br/><br/>The characters were ok, though, again, fairly typical, but my biggest issue was the way Conn, raised poor and uneducated, was naturally good at everything. He learns to read in about a day, and can memorize complicated spells after hearing them twice.<br/><br/>As for</span>
  <span id="freeText4340749705133713025" style="display:none">2.5<br /><br />A pretty decent story, if a little typical - orphan boy steals a wizard's locus magicalicus, which should kill him but doesn't. The wizard, intrigued, takes the boy in and the boy just happens to turn out to be a sort of chosen one figure. <br /><br />The characters were ok, though, again, fairly typical, but my biggest issue was the way Conn, raised poor and uneducated, was naturally good at everything. He learns to read in about a day, and can memorize complicated spells after hearing them twice.<br /><br />As for interactions, everyone sort of jumped to conclusions, and no one listened to anyone else. I guess, in a way, it makes sense for people to not listen to an untrained boy who used to be a thief but, still, it was annoying when Nevery knew something was going on, but refused to listen to Conn's ideas.<br /><br />Also, the writing was a bit meh. Very sort of clipped:<br /><br />"Then I heard it. Step step tap. Step step tap. edged back into my alley shadows to wait, and along he came. Old man, I thought. A bet, bearded, clock-wearing old croakety croak leaning on a cane. Climbing the steep street toward me. Muttering to himself. His purse, I decided, would be paying for my dinner, though he didn't know it yet."<br /><br />And she's fond of using terms like "light-feather fingers", "keen-gleam eyes" - that sort of thing.<br /><br />The story alternates between Conn's first person narration, and Nevery's journal, but both are written in a very clipped, matter-of-fact kind of style. <br /><br />But, for all that, it was a quick read, and rather fun, for all its flaws. </span>

<div id="review_152333360" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/152333360" />
    <a title="Roslyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/711951-roslyn"><img alt="Roslyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1278554725p2/711951.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/152333360?book_show_action=true">Mar 05, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Roslyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Roslyn" href="/user/show/711951-roslyn">Roslyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it

<span id="freeTextContainer539138512000487157">Charming, with hidden depths. It puzzled me a bit at first - the characters almost appeared superficial, but I suspected there was more, and there was. Loved the way the protagonist's POV interacts with the diary of another main character. Can't wait to read the next in the series.</span>

<div id="review_1991577148" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1991577148" />
    <a title="Kathy Davie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4222001-kathy-davie"><img alt="Kathy Davie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1285089902p2/4222001.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1991577148?book_show_action=true">May 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathy Davie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathy Davie" href="/user/show/4222001-kathy-davie">Kathy Davie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222001-kathy-davie?shelf=homey">homey</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222001-kathy-davie?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222001-kathy-davie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1991577148" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6862020857075904439">First in the Magic Thief fantasy series for middle-grade readers and revolving around a young pickpocket with potential.<br/><br/>In 2011, <em>The Magic Thief</em> was nominated for the Iowa Teen Award and also in 2009 for the E.B. White Read-Aloud Award.…<br/><br/><b>My Take</b><br/>…This reminds me of Angie Sage’s <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/series/44897-septimus-heap' title='Opens a list of books in Angie Sage's Septimus Heap series in Goodreads' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Septimus Heap</a> series, right down to the book size. Prineas, however, does have a different take on how magic works and who her major protagonist is. I enjoyed her dual first-person protagonist point-of-view with Conn, as it</span>
  <span id="freeText6862020857075904439" style="display:none">First in the Magic Thief fantasy series for middle-grade readers and revolving around a young pickpocket with potential.<br /><br />In 2011, <em>The Magic Thief</em> was nominated for the Iowa Teen Award and also in 2009 for the E.B. White Read-Aloud Award.…<br /><br /><b>My Take</b><br />…This reminds me of Angie Sage’s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/44897-septimus-heap" title="Opens a list of books in Angie Sage's Septimus Heap series in Goodreads" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Septimus Heap</a> series, right down to the book size. Prineas, however, does have a different take on how magic works and who her major protagonist is. I enjoyed her dual first-person protagonist point-of-view with Conn, as it gives us his worldly wise street thief perspective on his world, and Nevery’s perspective provides good back history.<br /><br />I got pulled in by that first paragraph with Prineas’ combination thought- and question-posing hook. As for changing the font and page background color for Nevery’s notes, that was a handy visual cue that the perspective was changing from Conn’s to Nevery’s. <em>Thank you!</em> I always appreciate an author making it easy for the reader [me!] to stay connected to the story. Although, I could wish the page color hadn’t been quite so dark. Maybe it’s just my old eyes…<br /><br />Prineas combines the ticking clock scenario with Conn having to “prove” himself with the plot coupon of Conn having to find his magicalicus locus while she beautifully integrates her info dumps throughout the story. There were a few plot twists, but no major issues. Just enough to give the story a bit more interest.<br /><br />Conn isn’t shy about speaking up for himself or for what he thinks, and Prineas uses the epiphany plot beat with that excellent point Conn makes on the truth about magic.…<br /><blockquote>”Spells are a language and we use it to tell the magic what to do.”</blockquote><b>The Story</b><br />…The boy has potential, but Nevery isn’t sure he’s worth the trouble. Nor does Nevery have the time to train an apprentice, not when he must discover why the city is losing its magic.<br /><br />Although…the boy was able to withstand his locus magicalicus. <em>Hmmm, maybe he should give him a try…</em>…<br /><br /><b>The Characters</b><br />…Connwaer “<strong>Conn</strong>” is between twelve and fourteen years old and a successful lockpick and pickpocket, most of the time. <strong>Black Maggie</strong> was Conn's mother and the one who taught Conn how to pick locks.<br /><br /><strong>Nevery Flinglas</strong> is a wizard who was banished from Wellmet 20 years ago after an experiment blew up. His <strong>locus magicalicus</strong> had been his <strong>great-great-aunt Alwae</strong>’s stone. <strong>Benet</strong> is hired muscle with a talent for knitting and baking. The house Nevery left behind, <strong>Heartsease</strong>, is falling to pieces. <strong>Lady</strong> is the cat.…<br /><br /><em>
  <b>Wellmet is…</b>
</em><br />……one of a loose confederation of cities, the Peninsular Duchies. It runs on magic and is ruled by <strong>Willa Forestall, the Duchess of Wellmet</strong>, who is based in the <strong>Dawn Palace</strong> in the well-off <strong>Sunrise</strong> neighborhood. <strong>Captain Kerrn</strong>, <strong>Farn</strong>, <strong>Jas</strong>, and <strong>Merik</strong> are guards.<br /><br /><em>Wellmet Academics is…</em><br />…headquartered on the islands which are the homes of the <strong>magisters</strong>, wizards, if you will. <strong>Magister Brumbee</strong> is the Master Wizard of the academy and is part of the council along with <strong>Periwinkle</strong>, <strong>Sandera</strong>, <strong>Pettivox</strong> who is also the court liaison, and <strong>Trammel</strong>, who appears to have some skill with healing.<br /><br /><strong>Lady Rowan Forestal</strong> is a regular student at the academy — and the duchess’ daughter — and has been set to mentor Conn. <strong>Keeston</strong> is Pettivox’s apprentice and a real jerk who has been partnered with Conn.<br /><br /><strong>Underlord Crowe</strong> is the crime lord of Wellmet with headquarters in <strong>Dusk House</strong> which is in the <strong>Twilight</strong> neighborhood of factories, warehouses, and the poor. He’s also Conn’s uncle.<br /><br />A <strong>locus magicalicus</strong> enables a wizard to focus magic and work spells. <strong>Slowsilver</strong> restrains magic, so a wizard can examine it. <strong>Embero</strong> is a dangerous spell. <strong>Micnu</strong> wrote a paper explaining how magic is created; he and <strong>Carron</strong> have written about magical nodes.…<br /><br /><b>The Cover and Title</b><br />…The cover is a textured deep and grayed royal blue with embossed gold frames and plaques. The title and author’s name are embossed in a deeper gold inside the plaques — top and bottom respectively. The center, inside its round, gold frame is a graphic of Nevery and Conn, using his street skills along with his locus magicalicus. On the left of the cover, just below the pivot of the conjoined frames <em>is</em> the leaf-shaped green and gleaming locus magicalicus.<br /><br />The title could go two ways, for there are indeed two thieves, and <em>The Magic Thief</em> could be the thief being reformed or the thief being born.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6862020857075904439" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_282360963" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/282360963" />
    <a title="Abby" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7574713-abby"><img alt="Abby" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1327963720p2/7574713.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/282360963?book_show_action=true">Feb 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Abby" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Abby" href="/user/show/7574713-abby">Abby</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7574713-abby?shelf=ya-lit-2012">ya-lit-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer282360963" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14786211802712566425">Plot Summary:<br/>The city of Wellmet is losing its magic and no one can seem to figure out why. It is up to a previously exiled wizard named Nevery and a young thief named Connwaer, to save the town from its untimely demise. The story tells of Connwaer’s search for his locus magicalicus, or the stone that allows wizards to harness magic’s power and how he enters into apprenticeship with the older wizard. He also helps Nevery solve the mystery behind the lost magic. <br/><br/>Main Characters:<br/>Connwaer: He is a </span>
  <span id="freeText14786211802712566425" style="display:none">Plot Summary:<br />The city of Wellmet is losing its magic and no one can seem to figure out why. It is up to a previously exiled wizard named Nevery and a young thief named Connwaer, to save the town from its untimely demise. The story tells of Connwaer’s search for his locus magicalicus, or the stone that allows wizards to harness magic’s power and how he enters into apprenticeship with the older wizard. He also helps Nevery solve the mystery behind the lost magic. <br /><br />Main Characters:<br />Connwaer: He is a young boy that was raised on “the wrong side of town”, quite literally. His mom dies while he is still young and he fends for himself in the “twilight” neighborhood. He has a strong will and does not lie. He is also eager to learn, and will not be entered into servitude.<br /><br />Nevery: Nevery is an old wizard, who 20 years prior, was exiled from Wellmet because he blew up his house and part of the palace. He is a bit of an ornery older man, who walks with a cane and believes that things are not always how they look.<br /><br />Benet: Benet is the “hired muscle” for Nevery and Connwaer. Even though he is hired more as a body guard, we find out that he also has excellent cooking and knitting skills.<br /><br />Key Issues: <br />Fantasy, Magic, Good vs. Evil, Changing your Destiny<br /><br />Other Interesting information: <br />I love how throughout the book, whenever Connwaer felt like he was not going to be allowed to continue his apprenticeship, or if Nevery used corporal punishment among other things, he had such a strong will and pride about him that he would say things like, “I would not be a servant, that would never do,” or “I just would not allow it.” He was quite daring for the time period that this seems to be set in. The reason that I gave this book four out of five stars was that I really did the novel, it had an interesting, page turning plot line, and the characters were funny. The book was a little slow going on the plot, but I would definitely want this book in my classroom, and would recommend it to others.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14786211802712566425" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_34804493" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/34804493" />
    <a title="Lucy " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45923-lucy"><img alt="Lucy " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1300985055p2/45923.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/34804493?book_show_action=true">Oct 08, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lucy " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lucy " href="/user/show/45923-lucy">Lucy </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45923-lucy?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45923-lucy?shelf=middlegrade">middlegrade</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer34804493" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9727809483785818965">Conn is a thief--a pickpocket, lockpick and gutterboy. Living in the Twilight, the seedy district of the magical city of Wellmet, there's not much else he could be. But when he picks the pocket of the wizard Nevery and comes out with Nevery's locus magicalicus, he's stolen more than he expected.<br/><br/>Nevery expects Conn to be dead--and fast--but when Conn doesn't die, Nevery decides to keep him around--just for a little while. Just until he figures out why not.<br/><br/>While Nevery may think that Conn is his s</span>
  <span id="freeText9727809483785818965" style="display:none">Conn is a thief--a pickpocket, lockpick and gutterboy. Living in the Twilight, the seedy district of the magical city of Wellmet, there's not much else he could be. But when he picks the pocket of the wizard Nevery and comes out with Nevery's locus magicalicus, he's stolen more than he expected.<br /><br />Nevery expects Conn to be dead--and fast--but when Conn doesn't die, Nevery decides to keep him around--just for a little while. Just until he figures out why not.<br /><br />While Nevery may think that Conn is his servant, Conn knows that he's really Nevery's apprentice--and that he is meant to be a wizard. But there are a few obstacles standing between Conn and his plans. He has to find his own locus magicalicus within thirty days, or he's out. And between going to school for the first time and trying to help Nevery solve the dangerously low level of magic in Wellmet, Conn is running out of time.<br /><br />This book is. so. good. Conn is utterly, ridiculously, wonderfully likeable. That's the first thing. Once you start reading his first-person narrative, you don't want to stop. And Prineas's fascinating magic system is clever. Best of all, Wellmet is a fully realized city in a fully realized world--and even as Conn only sees bits and pieces of it, we pick it up on the periphery of his vision--kind of like the way we learned about Lyra's Oxford in The Golden Compass. <br /><br />This book is the real deal. An honest to goodness great adventure, a feel-good fantasy read that you won't be able to stop reading and will be sorry once the book is over. <br /><br />Lucky for us, it's the first in a trilogy.<br /><br />So if you haven't read Sarah Prineas's The Magic Thief yet, why not? Get to it. You will not regret it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9727809483785818965" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_149179509" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/149179509" />
    <a title="Bette" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1809172-bette"><img alt="Bette" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1387055691p2/1809172.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/149179509?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bette" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bette" href="/user/show/1809172-bette">Bette</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1809172-bette?shelf=children-s">children-s</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer149179509" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17213259415330667643">I liked this book a lot. It's a bit derivative of JK Rowling's Harry Potter series. There is a wizard school, for instance, but the focus of the book on schooling isn't nearly as prominent as in Harry Potter. But overall, Prineas succeeds in creating a unique alternative fantasy world with an engaging protagonist. The main character, Conn, is a clever pickpocket and lock picker. He is "nosy," according to the wizard, Nevery, but it's his curiosity that leads him to solve the mystery of why the a</span>
  <span id="freeText17213259415330667643" style="display:none">I liked this book a lot. It's a bit derivative of JK Rowling's Harry Potter series. There is a wizard school, for instance, but the focus of the book on schooling isn't nearly as prominent as in Harry Potter. But overall, Prineas succeeds in creating a unique alternative fantasy world with an engaging protagonist. The main character, Conn, is a clever pickpocket and lock picker. He is "nosy," according to the wizard, Nevery, but it's his curiosity that leads him to solve the mystery of why the ambient magic in Wellmet is disappearing. Benet, the "muscle," reminds me a little of Butler in "Artemis Fowl"; Benet seems to be just muscle at first, but he turns out to have a good heart, as does Nevery. The relationship among the 3 grows as the story progresses. <br /><br /><br />The story-telling technique is inventive. It consists of Conn's first-person narrative interrupted periodically by Nevery's diary entries. This allows for humor since Conn at first thinks he's Nevery's apprentice, while Nevery keeps calling him a servant in his diary. There is actually quite a bit of humor in the book. Conn keeps eating Nevery out of house and home, i.e. <br /><br />My only objection to the book is that I found the magical language awkward. I kept having to stop to figure out how to pronounce the words for spells and magical objects, and they didn't seem to have a rhyme or reason, unlike Rowling's, which are Latin-based. Plus the spells themselves are very unwieldy. They are just a lot of letters strung together. <br /><br />But overall, I enjoyed the book a lot and would read the rest of the trilogy. It's a good addition to the fantasy of childre's fantasy lit.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17213259415330667643" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Hallie by: </span>
      Dorian
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1145657-hallie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1145657-hallie?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer88751157" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10806014261744266217">This one just felt right from the beginning and continued to hit me the right way throughout. It's a bit younger than I normally read, but the fact that I never felt the least bit less enjoyment from it says a lot.<br/><br/>It's extraordinary because if you set up the plot it sounds very, very old. Young boy, underdog of the first order (orphan, "gutterboy", pick-pocket), taken up, reluctantly, by an older wizard - a grumpy and often distracted one who ultimately comes to care for the boy. (I almost could</span>
  <span id="freeText10806014261744266217" style="display:none">This one just felt right from the beginning and continued to hit me the right way throughout. It's a bit younger than I normally read, but the fact that I never felt the least bit less enjoyment from it says a lot.<br /><br />It's extraordinary because if you set up the plot it sounds very, very old. Young boy, underdog of the first order (orphan, "gutterboy", pick-pocket), taken up, reluctantly, by an older wizard - a grumpy and often distracted one who ultimately comes to care for the boy. (I almost could see Nevery saying "Fool of a Took!" at some point.) And big threat to the city through loss of its magic which only the boy can figure out in time to save the day, using his magical talents and left-over thieving skills. <br /><br />BUT. Conn is one of the best characters I've encountered in a long time, and the super-restrained presentation of his real pain ends up being very effective. The magic was fun too, and all three of the male main characters being men of few words worked too. <br /><br />Lest it should seem that only the boys have any interesting parts, it's not the case! The ruler of Wellmet is a woman, and her daughter Rowan is another great character. That said, after Conn, my favourite is probably Benet, hired as a thug, pretty much, but a knitting, cooking sweetie. (Not that I'd say it to his face.)<br /><br />Finally - it's got runes for deciphering. I'd have loved them as a child and I still love them now. And the messages at the bottom of Nevery's journal are so much fun it's a nice touch.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10806014261744266217" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText2643230303571559661" style="display:none">The story is told in first person by Conn, the thief; through the journal of Mevery, the wizard; and in correspondence to and from him. Conn has forever been a thief, but when he steals a wizard's magic stone and nothing happens, the wizard takes an interest in the boy. Conn becomes Nevery's apprentice, an uneasy assignment for both the boy and his master. To be an apprentice and accepted by the council of wizards, Conn must first find his own magic stone, not an easy task. When Nevery is asked to find the reason for the city of Wellmet's loss of magic, Conn attempts to help the wizard, only to realize that he himself is in danger.<br /><br />Phineas has created a magical city and a cast of characters with sharp personalities. Conn is a completely honest thief, a hero with a tarnished past. At the academicos, he strikes up relationships with two students who each surprise the reader with who they are and what they become. Children will want to know more about Conn, Rowan, Benet, and Nevery.</span>

<div id="review_2616840903" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2616840903" />
    <a title="Devin Ames" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54397396-devin-ames"><img alt="Devin Ames" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1541377268p2/54397396.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2616840903?book_show_action=true">Dec 08, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Devin Ames" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Devin Ames" href="/user/show/54397396-devin-ames">Devin Ames</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2616840903" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10598206610755569889"> In the fantasy story <u>The Magic Thief</u> by Sarah Prineas, the city of Wellmet is losing it’s magic. Conn is a young pick-pocket and a thief, who is growing up alone on the streets of Twilight, dirty, in thread-bare clothes, just trying to stay alive. He picks the pocket of a wizard named Nevery and takes his locus magicalicus, a stone that focuses the magic of wizards. Each wizard has their own, unique locus magicalicus. Surprisingly, he lives after touching the stone. Nevery is fascinated, and de</span>
  <span id="freeText10598206610755569889" style="display:none"> In the fantasy story <u>The Magic Thief</u> by Sarah Prineas, the city of Wellmet is losing it’s magic. Conn is a young pick-pocket and a thief, who is growing up alone on the streets of Twilight, dirty, in thread-bare clothes, just trying to stay alive. He picks the pocket of a wizard named Nevery and takes his locus magicalicus, a stone that focuses the magic of wizards. Each wizard has their own, unique locus magicalicus. Surprisingly, he lives after touching the stone. Nevery is fascinated, and decides to find out why. He takes the boy home with him to serve as his apprentice. Although Conn is a thief, we come to realize, as does the wizard Nevery, that he’s actually good-hearted, honest and hardworking boy. As he learns about magic from Nevery and searches for his own locus magicalicus, he becomes suspicious of other wizards that he meets. Will he find the answer to why magic is dwindling in Wellmet? Will the answer be found before all magic is gone and the city dies? <br /><br /> I don’t read many fantasy books, but I chose to read this one because my students enjoy it. Prineas weaves a story full of magic and adventure that’s reminiscent of the Harry Potter series. Students would be able to easily relate to the likable main character, Conn and his quest to find answers. The book is full of action and some interesting plot twists along the way to keep students engaged. Prineas’s use of magic and spells in the book is metered, with magic being used at just the right time and in the right circumstances, perhaps giving the impression that magic isn’t to be taken lightly.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10598206610755569889" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2488422579?book_show_action=true">Aug 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca" href="/user/show/2988548-rebecca">Rebecca</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2988548-rebecca?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2488422579" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18338230055734478136">Very engaging opening to a series about a 'gutterboy', Conn, who becomes an apprentice to a Wizard in a city where the magic is fading.<br/><br/>There isn't a whole lot that's original here--Conn is the underestimated poor kid seemingly playing out of his league, Nevery is a grumpy old wizard ostracized by his peers, and the Duchess's daughter shows up to play tutor and get in on the action, but The Magic Thief is a fun ride. <br/><br/>Highly recommended. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Ddjf9Hnte6+v5acUcZ2PubAXJt1VKmUSYU9x0EBGAN8UPHkS/UFKgQCuX5l22u5FhdDYrTZOhksCnVg7JKvwQQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

  }

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('bookCover_6940291').observe('prototip:shown', function () {

            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
